### Post by Thylacine1 on 2014-04-26
Hi there,
I have been a user of Ubuntu 12.04 for a while, but am still feeling my way around. recently transfered my hard drives to another computer brought home from work. It all works well, but is not as fast as I had thought it would be, because on the face of it, the newer computer is significantly faster than what I was using previously. The CPU is an iCore 540 which is rated at 3.066 MHz.

As you can see on the accompanying screenshot, it is however running at around 1.1 MHz, and although no programs were running, of the 4 GB of RAM, around 3.6 Gigs are in use, or am I interpreting the data wrongly.

Thanks for any diagnostic help you can give me.

### Post by QIII on 2014-04-26
Your screenshot does not seem to be attached.

The fact that your CPU is running at that speed is similar to the way that the engine on your car idles when you are at a stop light.  There is no reason at all for it to run at the red line when you are sitting still.  This is expected.  Your CPU is being throttled as it should be when not under load.

We would have to see the screenshot to make a comment about the memory.

---

### Post by Yellow Pasque on 2014-04-26
Rather than a screenshot, give output of free command:
```
free -m
```
Most likely, you're interpreting it wrong (especially if you're used to Windows): [http://www.linuxatemyram.com/](http://www.linuxatemyram.com/)

---

### Post by tgalati4 on 2014-04-27
What is the speed of your hard disks?  Open a terminal:

```
sudo hdparm -tT /dev/sda
sudo hdparm -tT /dev/sdb
```
